  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f8ee3b2d-1a00-4348-9343-3152de258ca5'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/738609-what-order-are-you-supposed-to-read-rick">What order are you supposed to read Rick Riordan&#39;s books in? I&#39;ve started the Percy Jackson series but I want to know if I should finish this series and then start the heroes of Olympus series or can I start the heroes of Olympus series now.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_738609'><a id="like_count_community_question_738609" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/738609?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">9 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F17312201-the-son-of-sobek">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/738609-what-order-are-you-supposed-to-read-rick">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/738609-what-order-are-you-supposed-to-read-rick">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5675631-serena"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442713734i/5675631._UY100_CR39,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5675631-serena">Serena</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's best to start with the Percy Jackson and the Olympians series:<br/>The Lighting Thief<br/>The Sea of Monsters<br/>The Titan's Curse<br/>The Battle of the Labyrinth<br/>Th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's best to start with the Percy Jackson and the Olympians series:<br />The Lighting Thief<br />The Sea of Monsters<br />The Titan's Curse<br />The Battle of the Labyrinth<br />The Last Olympian<br /><br />(There is also The Demigod Files -which has short stories - and the graphic novels of The Lightning Thief, The Sea of Monsters and The Titan's Curse to look into. )<br /><br />The Kane Chronicles:<br />The Red Pyramid<br />The Throne of Fire<br />The Serpent's Shadow <br /><br /> (The Kane Chronicles: Survival Guide and the graphic novel of The Red Pyramid) <br /><br />The Heroes of Olympus:<br />The Lost Hero<br />The Son of Neptune <br />The Mark of Athena<br />The House of Hades<br />The Blood of Olympus <br /><br />(The Demigod Diaries and the graphic novel of The Lost Hero; the Percy Jackson-Kane Chronicles Crossover Stories: The Son of Sobek, The Staff of Serapis and The Crown of Ptolemy are collected in Demigods &amp; Magicians. There are also Percy Jackson's Greek Heroes and Percy Jackson's Greek Gods)<br /><br />*Rick's books are ongoing and these two series are of the same world as the later published works. <br /><br />The Trials of Apollo (Upcoming 5 Book Series):<br />The Hidden Oracle<br />The Dark Prophesy<br />The Burning Maze<br />The Tyrant's Tomb<br />The Tower of Nero<br />*Camp Half-Blood Confidential<br /><br />Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard (3 Book Series):<br />The Sword of Summer<br />The Hammer of Thor<br />The Ship of the Dead<br />*For Magnus Chase: Hotel Valhalla, Guide to the Norse Worlds 9 from the Nine Worlds<br /><br />There is also now "Rick Riordan Presents" written by other authors featuring works with mythologies around the world, but NOT CONNECTED to the Percy Jackson series and universe.<br /><br />Roshani Chokshi's Pandava Quartet<br />Aru Shah and the End of Time <br />Aru Shah and the Song of Death<br />Aru Shah and the Tree of Wishes<br />Aru Shah and the City of Gold<br /><br />J.C. Cervantes' Storm Runner Trilogy<br />The Storm Runner<br />The Fire Keeper<br />The Shadow Crosser<br /><br />Dragon Pearl by Yoon Ha Lee<br /><br />Carlos Hernandez's Sal and Gabi<br />Sal and Gabi Break the Universe <br />Sal and Gabi Fix the Universe<br /><br />Kwame Mbalia's Tristan Strong<br />Tristan Strong Punches a Hole in the Sky <br />Tristan Strong Destroys the World<br /><br />Race to the Sun by Rebecca Roanhorse<br /><br />Paola Santiago and the River of Tears by Tehlor Kay Mejia<br /><br />Serwa Boateng's Guide to Vampire Hunting by Roseanne A. Brown <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7487278399016721553">EDIT 6/20/13:<br/><br/>Well that was awesome......... I can't even express my pure love for this crossover. AND THEY TOTALLY GOT THAT THEY WERE FROM DIFFERENT MYTHOLOGIES! *Tears of joy* More! More! More! <br/><br/>What if when the 7 are closing the doors of death Percy calls Carter and.....? Ugh, I can't even. What if the future crossover book includes the Norse Mythology kids?! The best end to HoO would be all four mythologies uniting! 1. I mean.....   <span id="freeText7487278399016721553" style="display:none">EDIT 6/20/13:<br /><br />Well that was awesome......... I can't even express my pure love for this crossover. AND THEY TOTALLY GOT THAT THEY WERE FROM DIFFERENT MYTHOLOGIES! *Tears of joy* More! More! More! <br /><br />What if when the 7 are closing the doors of death Percy calls Carter and.....? Ugh, I can't even. What if the future crossover book includes the Norse Mythology kids?! The best end to HoO would be all four mythologies uniting! 1. I mean..... Can you just imagine all those awesome characters together..? :'D 2. All the bad guys joining forces would create the most bad-ass team of villains in history (LOKI!!!!!!)<br /><br />Also, this includes the first chapter of HoH so..... *Finds somewhere to cry some more* I just can't take the waiting....<br /><br />EDIT 5/20/13:<br /><br />Oh my sweet felafel that is one Percy-filled-awesome cover &lt;3.&lt;3 I'm actually surprised we even got a cover.. But we did... And look at Percy!!!! The gooey form that was my heart can barely wait. June 18. June 18. June 18. June 18..... &lt;\3<br /><br />EDIT 4/19/13:<br /><br />It includes an excerpt from the House of Hades!!!!!!! Can SOMEONE just put me into a coma till this comes out?!?!?!?!???!?!?!? Rick Riordan is evil. I bet it'll be like the Mark of Athena excerpt!!! I BET IT WON'T EVEN BE ABOUT PERCY AND ANNABETH IN TARTARUS!!!!!!<br /><br />I'm gonna go have a mental freak out in my closet because this little crossover of awesomeness just got a side of ice cream. And I really don't have any patience left. *Crying on the floor*<br /><br />EDIT 3/26/13: <br /><br />From Rick's website: <br /> Q. Would you ever do a crossover series with Kane characters and Percy Jackson characters?<br /><br />A. Because of your interest, I recently finished a short story called "The Son of Sobek" in which Carter Kane meets Percy Jackson. It's tons of fun! In the US, you can find this story in the back of the paperback edition of The Serpent's Shadow, available May 2013. It will also be available as an e-single later in the summer. More details to come. Some day, I might write a full-length novel crossover combining the two worlds, but remember that each novel takes one year to write, and I have a lot of other books I have to write first!<br /><br />YES WE GET A FULL-LENGTH NOVEL THIS ISN'T GONNA BE A COMPLETE COP OUT! I SEE THE LIGHT IN THIS DARK WORLD OF FANGIRL PAIN!<br /><br />ORIGINAL COMMENT/WHATEVER/BLAH:<br /><br />Hang on to my fangirl heart?! HOW CAN I?! A CROSSOVER IS COMING OUT! MY HEART HAS ALREADY THROWN ITSELF OFF A CLIFF INTO THE JAGGED ROCKS!! <br />*Sobbing*<br />I am so excited...... I'm already hyperventilating about the release of this book. OKAY, ENOUGH FANGIRLING!<br /><br />What do I expect? I expect lots of Percyness. I want sarcastic Percyness, as always. Also... since it's a short story, will there even be enough time for them to grasp that THEY ARE FROM DIFFERENT MYTHOLOGIES?! IF THEY JUST WALK AWAY CONFUSED, I WILL DIE .-. I've waited so long for this crossover that if Rick Riordan makes this really short and basically just an easy means out of having to write the crossover (That everybody was asking for).. Well.... I'm gonna cry, or scream, or most likely... die inside.<br />I was waiting for a crossover series.. So what I always imagined was something like Carter and the rest of them showing up at camp asking about the weird magical activity.. Then Idk.. Awesomeness. A collab fight? BUT WILL ANYTHING HAPPEN NOW?! And if it's only the two of them (Percy and Carter)...<br /><br />Idk.. Lets just wait and see. But right now I feel like a nervous ball of anticipation is knocking around my insides and when I finally get to read the short story, it will explode and I will die, painfully.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3383404213033373731"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/>A refreshing, short read from Uncle Rick the second. <3<br/><br/> Carter coincidentally (or perhaps not) meets Percy in Long Island as Carter tries to capture a huge monster crocodile called “petshuchos”, the son of the crocodile god, Sobek which Percy has been trying to seize for a long time already (Long Island being his home turf). Initially, the meeting wasn’t very civil because of unfamiliarity but they call a truce in a united mission to capture the monster. Of course, it’s Mr. Riordan so</span>
  <span id="freeText3383404213033373731" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br /><br />A refreshing, short read from Uncle Rick the second. &lt;3<br /><br /> Carter coincidentally (or perhaps not) meets Percy in Long Island as Carter tries to capture a huge monster crocodile called “petshuchos”, the son of the crocodile god, Sobek which Percy has been trying to seize for a long time already (Long Island being his home turf). Initially, the meeting wasn’t very civil because of unfamiliarity but they call a truce in a united mission to capture the monster. Of course, it’s Mr. Riordan so it ends with a cliffy! I didn’t expect any less! Lol! Told in Carter’s POV, this is a recommended fun read for fans of Carter Kane and Percy Jackson.^^<br /><br />You can read the short story <a href="http://ebook12.com/the-son-of-sobek/page-1-147146.htm" rel="nofollow noopener">here </a>. I hope this is legal because I don’t want to get sued or I guess if there’s anybody that should be sued, it’s the administrator of that site. Lol.<br /></span>

Both were absolutely confused at first, but<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ they seemed to get that its better NOT to interfere in each other worlds, even if its tempting for both of them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> . Percy was as usual sarcastic and brave, and Carter was also brave and calm and cool and trying to handle the situations in the worst situations. I gotta appreciate Rick in this crossover, because he had been very clever in ending their short awkward meeting, and even if he gives a hint that they can meet again, we definitely can not be sure, because, well, you'll read the ending yourself. He reminds me of one of his own characters in one of his books...his name is Quintus, and percy has mentioned of him that 'He fought the way some people play chess-like you couldn't see the pattern until he made the last stroke and won with a sword on your throat' Rick writes Exactly like that...so if you're all daydreaming about this story proceeding furthur, they'll all be lies because what Rick does is absolutely unexpected!!<br />More spoilers below<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ok, i dont know why but i was laughing hysterically when Percy compared Annabeth with Carter, when carter was Lecturing history to percy. And the fight, man THATS WHAT I CALL A FIGHT, even if the fight is with A DAMN CROCODILE BABY!!! One of my fav lines was when carter said 'Potassium and Water are harmless separately, but together they can make things go BOOM! Percy was water, i was potassium.'  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Now its absolutely Rick's choice to write more or not, because even by reading the crossover we can't say that Rick will write on it furthur *shrugs*. But Rick, if you're reading this ( calming my fangirl heart), THANKS A LOT! ITS A HIT!! Even if there wasn't somethings that i was soo keen to see....its Awesome!<br />---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><b>When i got to know about the crossover</b><br /><br />SHOOT!! I ws waiting for something like this for such a long time..and im getting it news now?? Damn! I wanna be in America..New York would ve best XD. Rick please please make it a blast like you do with each and every book of yours. I am especially excited.for <br /><br />1. Sadie vs. Clarisse. (leo would be awesome too.)<br />2. Nico vs. Walt(anubis..take your pick..they're in one body). Hazel Vs. walt would be fun too.<br />3. Sadie's funny dialogues on Romans!!<br /><br />But i think its only gonna be Percy vs. Carter!<br /><br />Rick...if you're 'luckily' reading this, you better make it awesome!! And plzz DON'T end the story in a cliffhanger like u did with the preview of this story And in the MOA (ur fans r still angry wid u fr THAT cliffhanger)!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1312124448602978085">The Son of Sobek (Percy Jackson & Kane Chronicles Crossover, #1), Rick Riordan<br/><br/>After hearing reports about magical disturbances in the Long Island area, Carter Kane goes to investigate. He is unexpectedly swallowed by an enormous crocodile in the marshes at the edge of Moriches Bay on Long Island's south shore while exploring, but is saved by a strange older teenager who forces the monster to regurgitate him. The teenager turns out to be Percy Jackson. After a brief disagreement that leave both c</span>
  <span id="freeText1312124448602978085" style="display:none">The Son of Sobek (Percy Jackson &amp; Kane Chronicles Crossover, #1), Rick Riordan<br /><br />After hearing reports about magical disturbances in the Long Island area, Carter Kane goes to investigate. He is unexpectedly swallowed by an enormous crocodile in the marshes at the edge of Moriches Bay on Long Island's south shore while exploring, but is saved by a strange older teenager who forces the monster to regurgitate him. The teenager turns out to be Percy Jackson. After a brief disagreement that leave both confused about the other's origins, Percy and Carter decide to team up to deal with the monster, which has left them and is terrorizing a nearby suburban neighborhood.<br /><br />Carter hypothesizes that the beast is a petsuchos, a son of the god Sobek and thus immortal and invincible unless the enchanted necklace that it wears, which is invested with the power of Sobek, is removed. The two work together to remove the necklace from the animal, and save the neighborhood and its residents. <br /><br />After the necklace is removed, the monster shrinks into a baby crocodile and the heroes head to a diner to talk. Percy and Carter are guarded about what they share, but devise a way to contact each other again if needed. they go their separate ways, and Carter takes both the crocodile and necklace back to the 21st Nome for safekeeping.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش روز هفتم ماه نوامبر سال 2017میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: پسر سوبک؛ نویسنده: ریک ریوردان؛<br /><br />اینبار «ریک ریوردان» تصمیم می‌گیرد که یونانی‌ها را با مصری‌ها رو در رو کند؛ در کتاب «پسر سوبک»؛ با اعلام اختلالات جادویی در «لانگ آیلند»، «کارتر کین (شخصیت وقایع نگاری کین)» برای بررسی به آنجا می‌رود، و با تمساحی غول‌آسا روبرو می‌شود، تمساح او را قورت می‌دهد؛ «کارتر» در حال گفتن کلمه‌ ی قدرت برای باز کردن راهش در دل تمساح بود، که «پرسی جکسون (شخصیت پرسی جکسون و المپی‌ها و قهرمانان المپ)» او را نجات می‌هد؛ ولی «کارتر» اشتباهاً کلمه‌ ی قدرتی که می‌خواست به تمساح بزند را به «پرسی» میزند و…؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15166697104267734651"><b>~3.5 stars~</b><br/><b>
  <i>Re-read 10/30/20</i>
</b><br/><br/>This was a fun and quick read. Not sure if it is something I needed, but I will litterly read anything Rick Riordan. I don't think I've ever read anything from him that I've disliked. I think the biggest thing I didn't like about this re-read was that my knowledge on the Kane Chronichals is fuzzy as it has been I think 3 years since I've last read it. Maybe I should have waited to read this after a re-read of at least The Red Pyramid. But it was a cool crossover. I</span>
  <span id="freeText15166697104267734651" style="display:none"><b>~3.5 stars~</b><br /><b>
  <i>Re-read 10/30/20</i>
</b><br /><br />This was a fun and quick read. Not sure if it is something I needed, but I will litterly read anything Rick Riordan. I don't think I've ever read anything from him that I've disliked. I think the biggest thing I didn't like about this re-read was that my knowledge on the Kane Chronichals is fuzzy as it has been I think 3 years since I've last read it. Maybe I should have waited to read this after a re-read of at least The Red Pyramid. But it was a cool crossover. I would have preferred for it to be from Percy's POV, because as much as I like Carter, Percy is my boi. Also if it would have been Carter x Annabeth and Sadie x Percy I would have liked that dynamic better because they are more similar that way. But I'm sure the Annabeth and Sadie short story is gonna be iconic.</span>

<div id="review_523746737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/523746737" />
    <a title="MOVED - CHECK BIO" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4593621-moved---check-bio"><img alt="MOVED - CHECK BIO" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426870313p2/4593621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/523746737?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MOVED - CHECK BIO" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MOVED - CHECK BIO" href="/user/show/4593621-moved---check-bio">MOVED - CHECK BIO</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Percy Jackson fans, Kane Chronicles fans, just about anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593621-moved---check-bio?shelf=rick-riodan">rick-riodan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593621-moved---check-bio?shelf=awesomest-books-ever-read">awesomest-books-ever-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593621-moved---check-bio?shelf=percy-jackson-demigods">percy-jackson-demigods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593621-moved---check-bio?shelf=boy-lead">boy-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593621-moved---check-bio?shelf=can-you-believe-how-freaking-awesom">can-you-believe-how-freaking-awesom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593621-moved---check-bio?shelf=cover-is-freaking-awesome">cover-is-freaking-awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer523746737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14829034211555837883">My reaction when I bought this book? Complete and total fangirl freakout(Consisting of squealing, screaming, yelling, dancing, giggling, and thanks the gods- Both Egyptian and Greek -that I had the money to buy it).<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Unlike Riordan's other stories, this one is a short story. The difference between a short story and a book/novel is this: <i>It is visibly shorter.</i> So if you buy this book and end up upset that it's short, it's your fault. Because in the blurb/description, it actually says</span></span>
  <span id="freeText14829034211555837883" style="display:none">My reaction when I bought this book? Complete and total fangirl freakout(Consisting of squealing, screaming, yelling, dancing, giggling, and thanks the gods- Both Egyptian and Greek -that I had the money to buy it).<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Unlike Riordan's other stories, this one is a short story. The difference between a short story and a book/novel is this: <i>It is visibly shorter.</i> So if you buy this book and end up upset that it's short, it's your fault. Because in the blurb/description, it actually says that this is a short story. Therefore, <b>do not throw a hissy fit because it is short. It's a <i>short story</i>. Hence the 'short' part!</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In this short story, Rick Riordan has made two of his protagonists, each from different book series and worlds, meet. Who are they, you ask? Carter Kane, head of the 21st Nome in Brooklyn. And Percy Jackson, son of the Earthshaker and hero of the second Titan War. ((No, I am not favoring Percy by putting that he's a hero. Carter's one too! He kicked snake booty.)) The story takes place on Long Island, where the two protagonists meet. <br /><br />Now, I'm willing to bet that you think the plot is very complex, because it's an Egyptian and Greek together. You, sir(I do not care what your gender is), would be wrong. The plot is simple, exciting, and made me unable to stop reading. Carter's investigating the Island when he hears about a monster sighting. There, he meets Percy, who is also trying to find the monster. The result? The two boys end up working together to stop the beast before it eats everyone.<br /><br />Okay, one of the things I love best about this book is.....It's told from Carter's Point-of-View!! And no, that is not a spoiler. I loved seeing Percy through Carter's eyes. It was just...Wow. Also, it's been so long since the Kane Chronicles series ended(About a year. But hey, that's long!), so I really enjoyed reading about/seeing him. :3 Carter is such a strong character and I feel like I can relate to him the most..At least with his personality, I can.<br /><br />Another thing I loved about the book was its humor. Oh my gosh, I loved its humor!!!!!!! It was full of hilarious moments that made me laugh so hard, I had to worry about being too loud, because someone in the room across from mine was asleep. :D :D :D :D </span>
  <a data-text-id="14829034211555837883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622795-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619456841?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/4622795-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619456841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer421892028136403083">Okay, so don't kill me but...I haven't read the Kane Chronicles.<br/>*flinches*<br/>I KNOW, I know I feel terrible and I should be executed for this unspeakable crime but, seriously, this short story convinced me to start reading them ASAP.<br/>This little crossover encounter was CRAY. I mean, we already know Percy Jackson is the baddest badass there is and I'm assuming Carter Kane would be the Egyptian equivalent. So together?<br/>The badassery is off the freaking charts.<br/>What I really loved was when they first met</span>
  <span id="freeText421892028136403083" style="display:none">Okay, so don't kill me but...I haven't read the Kane Chronicles.<br />*flinches*<br />I KNOW, I know I feel terrible and I should be executed for this unspeakable crime but, seriously, this short story convinced me to start reading them ASAP.<br />This little crossover encounter was CRAY. I mean, we already know Percy Jackson is the baddest badass there is and I'm assuming Carter Kane would be the Egyptian equivalent. So together?<br />The badassery is off the freaking charts.<br />What I really loved was when they first met and Percy is all laid back like 'Dude, I'm just trying to kill the monster." and Carter is angry-embarrassed like, "And who the HELL do you think you are?" and Percy is like "Um, I'm the guy who just saved your life. Your welcome."<br />Of course, I'm paraphrasing but you get it.<br />I just feel all warm and fuzzy inside. I had kind of a hard time holding it together long enough to write this review. This short story had Rick Riordan written all over it. He's so consistent with his writing and Percy is just SO PERCY. I mean COME ON:<br /><i>My vision cleared, and I saw two things that irritated me. First, the crocodile was charging me again. Second, my new friend Percy was just standing in the middle of the street, staring at me in shock. Apparently my combat avatar had startled him so much he’d forgotten his part of the plan.<br />‘What the creeping crud is that?’ he demanded. ‘You’re inside a giant glowing chicken-man!’</i><br />If that's not Percy Jackson, I don't know what is.<br />I also thought it was interesting to see Percy from yet another point of view. I thought it was kind of similar to seeing Percy through Jason's eyes considering that he, Percy and Carter are all sort of evenly matched in the leadership/power department. I guess every group of demigods has a Percy Jackson.<br />Anyway, this was really short but I have know idea how so much could be said and done in such a short story. It's awesome.<br />So, I'm gonna go get to know Carter a little better, now. I hope the Kane Chronicles brings me as much joy as PJO did. Wish me luck!<br />5 STARS!</span>
  <a data-text-id="421892028136403083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          marked it as to-read




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer533079660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17881031103918611402">I should have filmed my freak-out session once I found about this. I have to admit, I was a little disappointed by the second and third Kane Chronicles, but I still love the characters and idea. Ever since Carter mentioned seeing pegasi over the river, and Drew and Lacy were at Sadie's school dance... Well... I've been waiting for this a long time! :)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_619382042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619382042" />
    <a title="Jianred Faustino" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7607446-jianred-faustino"><img alt="Jianred Faustino" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433652423p2/7607446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619382042?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jianred Faustino" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jianred Faustino" href="/user/show/7607446-jianred-faustino">Jianred Faustino</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7607446-jianred-faustino?shelf=online-reads">online-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619382042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3272131923263731839">Now, first of, I just want everyone to know how I've been dying to have this cross-over ever since during Red Pyramid where Amos (I think) made some kind of reference that he's very much aware of the gods living in the Empire State building while looking at the building itself across from the East River (I think).<br/><br/>Sadly, I was not able to read the follow-up books of the Kane Chronicles.<br/><br/>Anyways, everyone's debating on what timeline was this meeting done. Imo, this was done before Hera whisked Perc</span>
  <span id="freeText3272131923263731839" style="display:none">Now, first of, I just want everyone to know how I've been dying to have this cross-over ever since during Red Pyramid where Amos (I think) made some kind of reference that he's very much aware of the gods living in the Empire State building while looking at the building itself across from the East River (I think).<br /><br />Sadly, I was not able to read the follow-up books of the Kane Chronicles.<br /><br />Anyways, everyone's debating on what timeline was this meeting done. Imo, this was done before Hera whisked Percy away to the Romans. My reasons?<br /><br />(1) <b>Percy thought that Carter might be a rouge demigod from Krono's army</b>. The way Percy mentioned the Kronos army like it was something fresh. Like it just happened. If this happened after Mark of Athena or maybe anywhere during the Heroes of Olympus series, Percy would have referred to Carter as Gaea's minions or something since the earth goddess is now much of a bigger threat than Kronos was. During the current timeline, the battling of Kronos was probably a year ago already.<br /><br />So, I'm assuming that maybe this happened like maybe a couple of days after the battle in Manhattan. Back in Last Olympian, I cannot remember whether there was reference on when the battle exactly ended but I think it was still summer. I think it ended on Percy's birthday though.<br /><br />(2) <b>The lack of mention to the hieroglyph on Percy's palm</b>. Sure the thing is invisible on his palm but I don't think the encounter with Carter is something that can be easily forgotten or not mentioned unless, you know, a certain goddess stole your memories and you are still in the middle of recovering them all back when you per say, <i>fell to Tartarus</i>?<br /><br />Honestly, the only thing that threw all this off?<br /><br />(1) <b>The mentioning of the Doors of Death</b>. If all my point up there is right, then why does Percy sound so sure of the Doors of Death? Like he already knows it. As far as I'm concerned, the only thing that was revealed in the Last Olympian was the 2nd Great Prophecy and nothing more.<br /><br />(2) In addition, <b>Carter thought of Percy as seventeen</b>. We all know that Percy is still sixteen and Carter might have thought of the wrong age since he was just merely sizing Percy up BUT...there's a big but there. What if that was some sort of clue left by Rick for us to tell that Percy is already 17 when he met Carter?<br /><br />I know, I know. The idea that this happened after Mark of Athena is really tempting. But will Rick really spoil us that much and tell us that both survived Tartarus and yet was not able to close the doors after torturing us for months?<br /><br />Besides, I already conjured up in my mind how Carter might be able to help the current war. He will be the wild card.<br /><br />It might not be the Romans that will help the seven demigods to close the doors. It could be the magicians. With their magic and everything, maybe they could do something about closing the doors on both side without sacrificing anyone. And for all we know, Hera could also be the one who organized the meeting between the two...no matter how unlikely that is. I have no idea if her power can stretched to the Egyptian world though.<br /><br />I better stop here now or might start thinking of other crazy ideas.<br /><br />I swear, Rick is making his readers smart by professional trolling. Or just by his genius plot.<br /><br />I really hate how much I love you Rick.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3272131923263731839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1362573073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1362573073" />
    <a title="Jesica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44637869-jesica"><img alt="Jesica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469336667p2/44637869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1362573073?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesica" href="/user/show/44637869-jesica">Jesica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1362573073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5918458026882589401"><blockquote>‘What are you?’ I demanded. ‘Part combat magician, part water elementalist? What nome are you with?’<br/>The kid laughed bitterly. ‘Dude, I don’t know what you’re talking about. I don’t hang out with gnomes. Satyrs, sometimes. Even Cyclopes. But not gnomes.’</blockquote><br/>It’s kind of short story by Rick Riordan where two of the heroes he wrote in two different series meets. Percy Jackson from <i>The Heroes of Olympus</i> series and Carter Kane from <i>The Kane Chronicles</i> series. Both are the lead character.<br/><br/>A giant Egyptian </span>
  <span id="freeText5918458026882589401" style="display:none"><blockquote>‘What are you?’ I demanded. ‘Part combat magician, part water elementalist? What nome are you with?’<br />The kid laughed bitterly. ‘Dude, I don’t know what you’re talking about. I don’t hang out with gnomes. Satyrs, sometimes. Even Cyclopes. But not gnomes.’</blockquote><br />It’s kind of short story by Rick Riordan where two of the heroes he wrote in two different series meets. Percy Jackson from <i>The Heroes of Olympus</i> series and Carter Kane from <i>The Kane Chronicles</i> series. Both are the lead character.<br /><br />A giant Egyptian crocodile rampaged at Long Island shore. Carter Kane, representing the Brooklyn House, went there to stop the croc he assumed was Sobek, the crocodile god. It wasn’t. He was so close to be defeated when Percy Jackson appeared. The monster had attacked camp half-blood too and eaten a pegasi. The meeting of the two heroes was quite disastrous. They needed to work together to beat the monster but they were not actually friendly to each other.<br /><br />This story is very fun for Rick Riordan fans (me :p). It’s one thing to read Percy and Carter in their own story but reading they meet each other is really exciting. <br /><br />The story is told from Carter’s POV. I’d always love Saddie’s POV than Carter’s in Kane Chronicles. I think Carter was kind of dull. But this story is not dull at all. It’s funny to see Carter a bit overwhelmed with the ‘camper boy’ with glowing sword who called his hawk avatar ‘giant glowing chicken man’. They even fought (for a VERY ridiculous reason) so for you who’s curious on who will win, Percy or Carter, demigod or magician, read this! The battle was really interesting.<br /><br />This short story is an exciting read recommended for Percy Jackson and Kane Chronicles fans. Like the other books by Rick Riordan (and this is the reason I adore Rick’s books), Rick managed to divide the role equally between both Percy and Carter so no one seemed more superior than the other. They really needed each other’s powers to beat their mutual croc enemy. It was hinted too that there’s someone trying to set the Greek and Egyptian against each other. And the end promised an exciting sequel :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="5918458026882589401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/580327322" />
    <a title="Sarah Banono" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12853631-sarah-banono"><img alt="Sarah Banono" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444275752p2/12853631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/580327322?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Banono" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Banono" href="/user/show/12853631-sarah-banono">Sarah Banono</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer580327322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16118121152916288994">HOLY GOODNESS.<br/>I found out that this book was coming out TODAY.<br/>And I was like OOOOOOOOOOOOHHHHH MAH GAAAAAAWD I CANNOT WAIT!!!!<br/>And I also found out that it comes out on June 18 as an e-book. <br/>And I also found out that if you buy it as an e-book, you get what Ricky here calls a "gift".<br/>And people, it is not ONLY gift, it is MORE than a gift.<br/>I call it THE BEST THANK YOU GIFT EVER!!!<br/>You're probably thinking: JUST TELL ME WHAT THE DARN THING IS ALREADY!<br/>Well…<br/>DRUM ROLL…<br/>IT'S AN EXCLUSIVE SNEAK PEEK CHAPTE</span>
  <span id="freeText16118121152916288994" style="display:none">HOLY GOODNESS.<br />I found out that this book was coming out TODAY.<br />And I was like OOOOOOOOOOOOHHHHH MAH GAAAAAAWD I CANNOT WAIT!!!!<br />And I also found out that it comes out on June 18 as an e-book. <br />And I also found out that if you buy it as an e-book, you get what Ricky here calls a "gift".<br />And people, it is not ONLY gift, it is MORE than a gift.<br />I call it THE BEST THANK YOU GIFT EVER!!!<br />You're probably thinking: JUST TELL ME WHAT THE DARN THING IS ALREADY!<br />Well…<br />DRUM ROLL…<br />IT'S AN EXCLUSIVE SNEAK PEEK CHAPTER FROM THE HOUSE OF HADES!!!<br />I said it guys! <br />It's from the HOUSE OF HADES.<br />It says so on his blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://rickriordan.blogspot.com/">http://rickriordan.blogspot.com/</a><br />Anyways, I'm über excited for this book (short story, whatever). I've always wondered how it would be if Carter and Percy met each other. When I read the excerpt of the Son of Sobek (EXCERPT: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/TheKaneChronicles/app_120262664819084">https://www.facebook.com/TheKaneChron...</a>), I was like WHOA, I WAS NOT EXPECTING THAT. Don't freak out; it's not bad, it's FABULOUS. I loved how the guys reacted to each other, Percy responding with his sarcastic remarks and Carter asking him who the HECK he was. It was hilarious! Every time I read the excerpt I'm like, ROFL!!!<br />I'm still laughing over it, it's just so funny,<br />Especially Percy.<br />Oh Percy, you always know how to make my day!<br />I should probably stop drooling over Percy.<br />Just read the excerpt, and when the short story comes out, read that too, guys.</span>

  <span id="freeText3950867491852374643" style="display:none">Lil' Excerpt:<br /><br />He stood to go. ‘One more thing,’ he said. ‘If this somebody, whoever threw us together … if he’s an enemy to both of us – what if we need each other to fight him? How do I contact you?’<br />I considered that. Then I made a snap decision. ‘Can I write something on your hand?’<br />He frowned. ‘Like your phone number?’<br />‘Uh … well, not exactly.’ I took out my stylus and a vial of magic ink. Percy held out his palm. I drew a hieroglyph there – the Eye of Horus. As soon as the symbol was complete, it flared blue, then vanished.<br />‘Just say my name,’ I told him, ‘and I’ll hear you. I’ll know where you are, and I’ll come meet you. But it will only work once, so make it count.<br />...<br />Whoever brought Percy and me together, whoever orchestrated our crossing paths … it smacks of Chaos. I can’t help thinking this was an experiment to see what kind of havoc would result. Potassium and water. Matter and antimatter.<br />Fortunately, things turned out okay.<br />But next time … well, I’m afraid we might not be so lucky.<br />Somewhere there’s a kid named Percy with a secret hieroglyph on his hand. And I have a feeling that sooner or later I’ll wake up in the middle of the night and hear one word, spoken urgently in my mind:<br />Carter.<br /><br />IS IT JUST ME OR DOES THIS HINT AT A NEW SERIES WITH A FUSION OF THE TWO?! eh? eh? anyone?!<br /><br />*grinning like a happy idiot* *realization dawns* *internal panic attack* *crying* *mental breakdown* *MORE PERCY*</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uo/e9WEfVYeG4TzGpCjhsiDDxml5lxtGVbeX5iVyfetRdt7d+c2yH7TAH7rmUg6FpakZ5eQYKbyGrgsi+CNzwA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DBoCNC0WkFqRyOfqNQGpPJPbrJR9/7X24XmGK/eED+Xn4wIctcR3wqPpxJZ3e0YLFrFzGOBwhwwyYBrvKtUBzg==')})
  }
//]]>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_18752963').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_18752963').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_18752963').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>
